< review>
We really enjoyed the food,  very tasty.  The service was excellent.  The quality of the food is excellent.  The waitress was very helpful with suggestions of very tasty dishes.  We could also order dishes not on the menu such as "Chinese Broccoli with Hoisin Sauce",  one of our favorites usually not on the menu at most Chinese restaurants.  We also found the prices  reasonable for the quality and quantity of the food.  We will be returning. Also, the one bad review was because the restaurant only had canned soda and didn't offer refills. I don't go to a good Chinese restaurant to drink soda. They give you all the  tea and water you want.</review>

< Text>
Most chinese restaurants I've been to, you would expect your entree in a simple platter. Not this place.  I ordered the Dragon and Phoenix and expected just that but these folks went all out to make an art show with their presentation.  The food is great, prices are appropriate and wait times are minimal. Their "dinner for one" option is perfectly portioned so that you can eat half of the entree and be satisfied while bringing the rest home for a second bite. Bottom line, I like this place and will come by more often.<//Text>

<user>107434908954743368047</user>< Name>
Stocks Huskies (Stocks and Huskies)< /Name>
< Date>
1492665741990<//Date>
< rate>
2< /rate>
< text>
Came in and it was a like a morgue. No music, no talking, no acknowledgement from the chef or waitress. Somewhat off-putting.

Ordered the Fried Shrimp (which has imitation shrimp) ... don't order this. Ever. Tastes like fried used gum. Absolutely terrible.

Got the following rolls:

Spicy Tuna - not good, put together terribly, bland taste for a SPICY roll

Ninja - alright taste, yet not something I would order again, put together terribly, has a slightly crunchy texture that gives it a good mouth feel

Golden Dragon - Order this. Now. It is a cooked roll, but this is the only saving grace of the night! Put together nicely, has a nice, non-greasy flavor, and it does not have a weird aftertaste.

Also, no wasabi or ginger served with the sushi ... out of the thirty or so hibachi/sushi spots I have been to in my life, I have never had to ask for wasabi. And it seemed like the chef was slow to give it to us.

The check comes out fast though, so a star for that in case you need to leave fast.

And new update ... my wife also felt queasy after eating here. I have an iron stomach, but that bodes badly about whether we will ever go back.

A lot of things going wrong here, but maybe they will be different if I try them again in a couple of years or so after getting a new chef.<//text>

<rate>5< /rate>< Review>
My family and I were going to a different Sushi Place, but they were closed last night, so my son googled  for close by Sushi restauranr and we went to Le Sushi. Tiny restaurant and I was hesitant, but wow, did we get a surprise. First of all, since I am allergic to Iodine, I told the hostes, that we needed to seperate anything that had shellfish in it. She said not to worry, this is a Kosher restaurant, no shellfish anywhere. I am in heaven without a worry. Then the food arrived and one roll was better than the other, to finish it of, we asked the chef to make us something excellent, since is was my birthday. We were so impressed. The food was 5+ stars. If you want good Sushi, don't bother - if you want excellent Sushi run, it is a tiny place and you might not find a place to sit if you wait too long. I loved this place and it is my favorite from now on!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!</Review>

<Date>1576673621381< /Date><rate>4</rate>< review>
Resident is a leftover star from the dot-com boom-bust days - all these years and still going strong.  The place is nice enough and gets pretty packed during weekday nights, composed of business casuals, hipsters, and the occasional influx of nametag-wearing convention goers.  The music can be quite good but the sound system and acoustics of the place could use some work.  A great place for people watching and/or to hang out if you don't mind having to talk much louder than usual.</review>

People come to the Arts District looking for an authentic "Arts District Vibe". As someone who has lived in this part of downtown for almost 20 years, I can tell you that The Resident totally captures the feel of the old arts district before it became an over priced millennial nightmare. Tim and Bridget are the real deal and you can feel the care they put into the place from the overall layout of the place, to the wonderful details of the decor. The Resident was designed by artists, for artists but everyone is welcome.<//review>

< review>
PRO: Great food truck, neat hipster & industrial looking outdoor large private patio. BBQ pulled pork & chicken wrap we're very tasty! Feels you're in someone's large back yard in Venice Beach. Inside, good size stage. Smoking allowed & an entire table was openly smoking joints when we went for drinks/dinner. Nice website for photos and info.

CON: Overpriced on everything, poorly maintained (for a new gentrified venue), limited parking, & short staffed. You'll drop $120 easy (2 people) at a very casual place. Many "atmosphere" items not working or set up at night, like broken patio lights, bathroom sign half broken, fire pits off on a cold night; it took several requests and +20mis for staff to find the right person to turn them on & cover other positions (bartender had to work door & delay drinks so security could start the pits). Tasty cocktails on tap, but mostly ice & overpriced by almost double for this part of town and simple refurbished venue.

We'd go again to see music, but I'd save my $$ and eat/drink elsewhere after trying it once for the full experience.</review>

<text>What a great space! The patio is friendly and welcoming, with a food truck on one side and the bar on the other, offering good seating options conducive to good chats among friends as well as mingling with others. Gin & Tonics are also quite generous :-)< /text><Date>1528666519549<//Date></record>
</dataset><record>
<Name>William Dempsey< /Name>< Text>
The outdoor courtyard at the Resident rivals any other in LA for beauty, a sense of peace and place (feeling like you really are in the middle of the metropolis), and the casual feel of a beer garden. Given it's proximity to the arts district and Little Tokyo, this bar/eatery/venue is probably one of the best situated in all of LA. Reasonably priced cocktails (try the London Calling!) for LA standards at a hipster joint (~$12 at this posting), and a great small floor space and stage for live music. The on-site food truck makes tasty (if a bit salty) food - some nice options (I think a lot are potato focused) and I remember a really great grilled cheese sandwich. Friendly and chill staff/bartenders. I've never been on the weekend, but during the week, this spot is pretty much the perfect place to spend some time with friends!<//Text>

<rating>5</rating>< Text>
Came here on a Saturday night at about 10:00 pm and stayed the rest of the night. The vibe at the Resident is very relaxed but fun. The music is great and definitely adds to the ambiance. There are two parts to the Resident. One section is the outdoor seated section, and they have plenty of seating to relax and enjoy a cocktail or some food from the food truck. The second section, I have not been into, but learned from an employee, that weather there is a cover charge varies from night to night depending on the event or Band that is playing that night. Overall if you are looking for a relaxed place to enjoy a drink, catch up in the evening while still being out and about, this is definitely the place.<//Text>

<text>Took some time on my spring break to get out of Burbank and enjoy some of the downtown Los Angeles area.  A friend and I decided to check out the Samskara 360 immersive art experience so why not stop here for a drink.  We were saving our appetites for after the art exhibit so we just came in to wet our whistles.  The have a truck for drinks and a truck for some grub. It would be very easy to sit and chill here for a couple of hours sipping cold drinks and eating some food.  The food looked good and the people eating it looked happy. < Review>
Damn I almost don't want to put a review because this place has the best layout and atmosphere PLUS the bartenders KNOW what's up. I have to give a shout-out to the Korean bartender I think named Brandon who is definitely good at what he does; this guy takes his job seriously (other Bartenders seem to take it seriously too). I recommend his old fashioned, it is so legit.

Great venue to bring a date to have a  chill night with some drinks and music. The outdoor area basically feels like a backyard hangout with pretty lights that girls like. When you bring a date start out in the quiet outside area where you can talk and connect with your date, then take her/him to the game area throw some sand bags around and get that bond with some high fives, next grab a beer outside in the beer garden or get some liquor inside from the great bartenders before casually dancing and bumpin' yo head to the music until ya'll are buzzed, and I suggest finishing up with a kiss in one of the corners inside.

The crowd is very hipster and friendly, good mix of people of all races, just a great friendly, chill venue with great drinks. I recommend it, I am definitely coming back with my GF when we need a quality bartender without crazy high prices.<//Review>
